<rate>5<//rate>< review>
I'm a filmmaker and I love The Prospect Studios (also known as ABC Television Center, a lot containing several television studios located at 4151 Prospect Avenue in the Los Feliz neighborhood of Los Angeles, at the corner of Prospect and Talmadge Street (named in honor of silent screen star Norma Talmadge), just east of Hollywood. I work here on General Hospital and I enjoy it. For more than 50 years, this facility served as the West Coast headquarters of the American Broadcasting Company before the network moved its main headquarters to the Walt Disney Studios in Burbank, California. From 1949 to 1999, ABC-owned Los Angeles television station KABC-TV was also located there. Truly inspirational. The station moved to a new state-of-the-art facility located on a portion of Disney's Grand Central Creative Campus (GC3) in nearby Glendale, California, in December 1999. The Walt Disney Company, which acquired ABC in 1996, continues to own and operate the facility to this day. I'm looking forward visiting again. Best, George Anton ANTFLIX<//review>

<user>117376774983242966176<//user>< user_name>
Alexis Osuna<//user_name>
<Time>1559516707287<//Time><Rating>4</Rating>< Review>
I love this place and the owner of the restaurant is a really cool guy. Nice vibe, nice service, but there are some important things I need to address.

1.) Understaffed. One man running the show is amazing when it comes down to getting the job done right. However, when it gets busy, customer's suffer. Either the food takes too long or the service is rushed. Be aware that summer attracts more people so you can expect a wait.

2.) Quality of food. The quality is amazing quite honestly. However, the raw meats are sub par. I love sushi and I found myself feeling unsatisfied with what I got (I tried two different sushies).

If you come here, I HIGHLY recommend trying the grilled food and their tacos. Amazing tacos and their unique drinks are probably the best that I've had in a while.</Review>

<Name>Jon M<//Name>< time>
1504274547014</time>
< Rate>
3</Rate>
< Review>
The good: it's a really good spot with inventive food. Tacos are on par with what you would find at Puesto. Lots of variety: poke, sushi, tacos, hand rolls, etc.
The bad: it's a bit pricy. $5 a taco, $12 a roll, etc. That's on par with Puesto, Coasterra, Harney Sushi, Hane, etc. But comparatively the ambiance leaves a lot to be desired. It's basically a converted tiny house, and you're eating on the "porch" with Surfboards as tables. All while facing a busy street. It's a very small eating area. I first went there with a group of 5. We had to go somewhere else because there was not enough space.
Summary: its like upscale dining meets beach shack, at upscale dining prices. With the small dining space, I wish they had more items that would be good for take out and priced better, so I can quickly pick it up and go back to work.</Review>

<Rating>3</Rating>< Review>
This gas station/truck stop is the busiest that I have ever seen. There is a continuous flow of rigs, trucks, and cars, in and out of this location. Therefore a continuous cashflow and a cash cow.
Then why are the fuel prices and store items priced higher than most convenience stores and gas stations? Obviously the owner has a monopoly here and likes to take advantage and gouge people.
There are public restrooms here and even a shower available for $8.00 which is cool.
The truck drivers can park their tractors in the back parking lot if they are detached from their trailers.
There are a few tractor trailer mechanics right next door for convenience.
There is also no shortage of "ladies of the night" available for truckers even in the daytime hours.
So I have given you the pros & the cons on this place....you decide if you want to pay the price.<//Review>

I had an experience a few days ago at Dr. Benedict's office that perfectly sums up why I think so highly of her dentistry. My bitewing x-ray showed a spot that concerned Dr. Benedict. < Review>
I've been here a number of times (lunch and dinner, over the past 3 years or so) and have always had a great experience. The decor isn't much to look at, but all of the food I've had has been extremely fresh and well-prepared. The buffet has a good variety, and all of the fresh veggies are beautiful. And you can't beat the price! Added bonus - I've got fairly serious food allergies, and the way they heat the food, it keeps your stuff on a single space on the griddle. I've been to other Mongolian places where they move the food across the whole griddle, so your stuff gets a lot of contamination from other peoples' plates, but here, your food stays on one section of the griddle until it is done.< /Review>

< Review>
I can see why there are so many varied reviews. This was my first time going to Church's Chicken since I was a kid. I can't complain too much! I was only in line for a hot minute, I ordered the three piece and a biscuit for 2.99 and they gave me an extra piece of chicken without my asking. The skin was really tasty and crispy, the meat itself could have cooked just a little bit longer for me and dried out just a little bit. The biscuit had great flavor-  I enjoy my food cooked a certain way, and the biscuit had an interesting little crisp to it which I really enjoyed, although I could totally understand if others might consider the biscuit too "hard"...The server was nice and a little silly, but he's just a kid so it was fine. Overall it was a nice first experience, would  I go back? Yes I would.</Review>
